            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             The Detroit Lions Will Miss the Playoffs
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="The Detroit Lions Will Miss the Playoffs" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/277/hi-res-151012532_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Gregory Shamus/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Teams that increase their win total by four or more games from year one to year two typically finish somewhere in the middle in year three, simply because they typically overachieved in year two.
           </p>
           <p>
            The
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1279922-detroit-lions-roster-2012-latest-news-cuts-preseason-predictions">
             Detroit Lions
            </a>
            had what was probably a career year from both
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/matthew-stafford">
             Matthew Stafford
            </a>
            and Calvin Johnson in the year of the quarterback. If both duplicate their success again in 2012, I will admit that Im wrong, but I think thats just asking too much.
           </p>
           <p>
            The offensive line is one of the weaker units in the gameespecially the tackles, who wont be doing Stafford any favorsand the defense did give up nearly 400 points last year, finishing 23rd in scoring defense, 23rd in total defense and 30th in average net passing yards allowed per attempt.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Chicago Bears are an improved team, and the
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1280109-green-bay-packers-roster-2012-latest-news-cuts-preseason-predictions">
             Green Bay Packers
            </a>
            are one of the two or three best teams in the league, so I expect the Lions to finish around the middle of the pack at 8-8.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-33 cf display-none " data-page="33">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Ryan Tannehill Will Have a Truly Miserable Season
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Ryan Tannehill Will Have a Truly Miserable Season" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/278/hi-res-150705392_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Joel Auerbach/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Theres not a lot to like about the Miami Dolphins heading into 2012. They jumped the gun and took quarterback Ryan Tannehill after whiffing on Peyton Manning. They made the dumbest move of the offseason by signing Chad Johnsonalthough fortunately they righted the wrong by releasing him.
           </p>
           <p>
            They traded starting corner Vontae Davis to the
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1280152-indianapolis-colts-roster-2012-latest-news-cuts-preseason-predictions">
             Indianapolis Colts
            </a>
            . And they already decided theyre going with rookie Tannehill as their starter even though hes probably not ready to start in this league for two seasons at least.
           </p>
           <p>
            Tannehill will be throwing passes to guys like Legedu Naanee, Brian Hartline, Davone Bess and Marlon Moore. His running back,
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/reggie-bush">
             Reggie Bush
            </a>
            , is coming off a career year, and last years draft pick (Daniel Thomas) looks awful. Oh, and the offensive line rated as the eighth-worst pass-blocking unit in the league last year,
            <a href="https://www.profootballfocus.com/data/by_team.php?tab=by_team">
             per Pro Football Focus
            </a>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            Dont pick Tannehill in fantasy football, and if youre a Dolphins fan, plan something else on Sunday afternoons so you dont have to watch.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-34 cf display-none " data-page="34">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             The Carolina Panthers Will Lead the NFL in Rushing Yards
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="The Carolina Panthers Will Lead the NFL in Rushing Yards" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/279/hi-res-150872133_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Zelevansky/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The Carolina Panthers have two running backs both locked up to long-term deals and a quarterback who runs the ball more than anyone else at his position in the league.
           </p>
           <p>
            Thats the recipe for a ground game that will put up 2,500 or more yards, and I think the 2012 Panthers will move the ball on the ground as well as any team in the game (especially because I see Cam Newton taking a step back as a passer).
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-35 cf display-none " data-page="35">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Matt Ryan Will Be the NFL's Fourth-Best Quarterback by the End of the Season
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Matt Ryan Will Be the NFL's Fourth-Best Quarterback by the End of the Season" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/280/hi-res-150705390_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Joel Auerbach/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Since the Atlanta Falcons drafted
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/matt-ryan">
             Matt Ryan
            </a>
            with the third overall pick of the 2008 NFL draft, hes been a terrific quarterback, but he hasnt quite taken that leap into the elite conversation.
           </p>
           <p>
            Much of the blame has been for his lack of playoff success (although youll have to excuse him for losing games when his defense gives up an average of 34 points per game).
           </p>
           <p>
            However, save for a sophomore slump, Ryan has improved his numbers every year. His passing yards, passing touchdowns and passer rating have gone up every year other than his second, and he now has a stud receiver in Julio Jones to go with Roddy White and Tony Gonzalez.
           </p>
           <p>
            Factor in that Michael Turner is regressing and the Falcons will have to pass more than everand that two of the other three teams in the NFC South ranked in the bottom six in the league in scoring defenseand that could be the recipe for a 4,800-yard, 36-touchdown season from Ryan.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-36 cf display-none " data-page="36">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             The Tampa Bay Buccaneers Will Be the NFLs Surprise Team
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="The Tampa Bay Buccaneers Will Be the NFLs Surprise Team" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/281/hi-res-150990351_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Rob Carr/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            I dont like picking a surprise team simply for the sake of the fact that there will be a surprise team (because there always is).
           </p>
           <p>
            That said, I really think the Tampa Bay Buccaneers will make major strides in 2012. They were a 4-2 team last year before they rolled over and played dead to get Raheem Morris fired.
           </p>
           <p>
            Josh Freeman will have to show whether he more resembles the quarterback that played at a Pro Bowl level for all of 2010 or the one that struggled mightily for all of 2011 (and as a rookie back in 2009). He has some significant offensive additions thoughthe Buccaneers signed Vincent Jackson to a five-year deal, drafted running back Doug Martin in the first round and signed All-Pro guard Carl Nicks in free agency.
           </p>
           <p>
            They grabbed college footballs top safety in Mark Barron to help shore up a unit that allowed nearly 500 points last yearalthough how many of those points were simply because they just gave up? With new coach Greg Schianoa no-nonsense disciplinarian whipping the players into shapetheir defense should more rival the 2010 unit that ranked ninth in the league in scoring defense.
           </p>
           <p>
            They also have the
            <a href="http://espn.go.com/blog/nflnation/post/_/id/56896/2012-nfl-strength-of-schedule" target="_blank">
             sixth-easiest schedule
            </a>
            in the league. It really will come down to the play of Freeman at quarterback, although an improved performance from the dreadful linebacker corps would go a long way too.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-37 cf display-none " data-page="37">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             If Youre Expecting RGIII to Be Cam Newton, Youre Going to Be Disappointed
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="If Youre Expecting RGIII to Be Cam Newton, Youre Going to Be Disappointed" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/282/hi-res-150739319_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Patrick McDermott/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Robert Griffin III has so much in common with Cam Newton that people are thinking RGIII is the new Newton.
           </p>
           <p>
            Both dominated in college football and won the Heisman Trophy before declaring for the NFL draft. Each was largely a one-year wonder. Each is a running quarterback who also can pass with the best of them.
           </p>
           <p>
            Newton passed for over 4,000 yards and accounted for 35 total touchdowns. Thats high expectations for RGIII, and he wont have the benefit of playing out-of-shape defenses after a lockout-shortened offseason. He also plays the NFC East, which features unstoppable defensive lines in the New York Giants and Philadelphia Eagles, plus a much-improved secondary in the Dallas Cowboys.
           </p>
           <p>
            Griffin doesnt have great weapons around him; Santana Moss is no longer a No. 1 receiver and the Washington Redskins are kidding themselves if they think Pierre Garcon is a legit starter. I envision Griffin playing conservative football, running frequently and finishing with somewhere around 15 touchdowns and 10 interceptions on a 5-11 Redskins team.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-38 cf display-none " data-page="38">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Patrick Peterson Will Become a Shutdown Corner
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Patrick Peterson Will Become a Shutdown Corner" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/283/hi-res-hi-res-136062951_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Christian Petersen/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            As a rookie in 2011, Patrick Peterson didnt show much as a corner, contrary to what people think. Peterson allowed more passing yards (834) than all but two cornerbacks in the NFL, getting torched for 7.69 yards per attempt and five different games of at least 80 receiving yards allowed.
           </p>
           <p>
            Peterson fared better down the stretch, routinely covering the other teams No. 1 receiver and allowing just 134 receiving yards in his final four games. He made the Pro Bowl because of his impressive punt returning skills (four touchdowns), but his coverage skills left something to be desired.
           </p>
           <p>
            I think he will take the step to being elite in 2012 though. After all, the Cardinals picked him fifth overall because of his amazing cover skills in college, and Peterson plays behind a very good defensive line that will get pressure on the opposing quarterback and make life easier for him.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-39 cf display-none " data-page="39">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">

             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Chris Johnson Will Bounce Back in 2012
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Chris Johnson Will Bounce Back in 2012" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/284/hi-res-150436748_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Al Messerschmidt/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            When people got on Chris Johnsons case for his slump following his 2,000-yard season, it bothered me. Of course hes not going to duplicate a 2,000-yard season; thats just setting the bar too high.
           </p>
           <p>
            What he did do1,364 rushing yards, 11 touchdowns, 4.3 YPC and a Pro Bowl appearancewas terrific, especially considering the quarterback situation was subpar with Vince Young and Kerry Collins.
           </p>
           <p>
            Last year though, CJ2K became CJ2YPC, as he consistently showed the world that he had no interest in playing football now that he had gotten paid ($53 million over four years, $30 million guaranteed). Johnson has looked good this preseason though, and the Tennessee Titans made an underrated acquisition during the offseason when they signed future Hall of Fame guard Steve Hutchinson to help the running game.
           </p>
           <p>
            I think Johnson has a chance to win the rushing title, although I think a top-five finish is more realistic. Still, 1,300 or more rushing yards on 4.5 yards per carry and 10 to 12 touchdowns on the ground is reasonable.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-40 cf display-none " data-page="40">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">

              <span class="aquo">

            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Charles Woodson Will Make the Pro Bowl at Safety
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Charles Woodson Will Make the Pro Bowl at Safety" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/296/hi-res-135518563_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jonathan Daniel/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The Green Bay Packers have moved Charles Woodson to safety as he enters his 15th NFL season, and I dont think Woodson will miss a beat.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Packers really need a solid season from him considering former All-Pro safety Nick Collins was released after a neck injury and the secondary was torched repeatedly last season. The return of B.J. Raji as an elite defensive tackle and the addition of USC pass-rusher Nick Perry will help Woodson too.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             People Will Realize John Skelton Isnt Much Better Than Kevin Kolb
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="People Will Realize John Skelton Isnt Much Better Than Kevin Kolb" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/285/hi-res-120506938_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Christian Petersen/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            I certainly dont blame Arizona Cardinals fans for wanting someone other than Kevin Kolb to play quarterback for their team. The fact that Ken Whisenhunt gave him a five-year contract with $12 million guaranteed should cost Whisenhunt his job.
           </p>
           <p>
            But do Cardinals fans really want John Skelton? He saw some fourth-quarter success in 2011, but how many quarterbacks can repeat that success two years in a rowwithout really being that good? Skeltons statistics from 2011: 54.9 completion percentage, 11 TD, 14 INT and a 68.9 passer rating that actually stands at 12.2 points behind the mark Kolb put up last year.
           </p>
           <p>
            Skelton did win more games, as he was 5-2 while Kolb was 3-6, but the Cardinals defense also gave up no more than 23 points in any of Skeltons starts while averaging 19 points allowed. For Kolb, they gave up 30 or more in four straight games and averaged 24 allowed.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-42 cf display-none " data-page="42">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             A Record 11 Quarterbacks Will Pass for 4,000 Yards
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="A Record 11 Quarterbacks Will Pass for 4,000 Yards" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/286/hi-res-136068060_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Wesley Hitt/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            List of quarterbacks that will pass for 4,000 yards in 2012:
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/aaron-rodgers">
             Aaron Rodgers
            </a>
            , Tom Brady,
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/drew-brees">
             Drew Brees
            </a>
            , Matt Ryan, Eli Manning,
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/tony-romo">
             Tony Romo
            </a>
            , Matthew Stafford, Jay Cutler, Philip Rivers, Josh Freeman and Joe Flacco.
           </p>
           <p>
            That will set the record, and I think several more will come close to 4,000 without quite reaching the mark (Andrew Luck, Peyton Manning, Michael Vick and Matt Schaub).
           </p>
           <p>
            The NFL is more of a passing league than ever, and theres a reason teams are switching to three-corner defensive backfields and two-tight end offensive formations.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-43 cf display-none " data-page="43">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             JPP Will Lead the NFL with 20 Sacks
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="JPP Will Lead the NFL with 20 Sacks" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/287/hi-res-150461103_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Drew Hallowell/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            I think Jason Pierre-Paul will be even better in 2012. He had 16.5 sacks as a second-year player in 2011, helping the New York Giants win the Super Bowl while making Philadelphia Eagles fans everywhere resent Brandon Graham for going two spots ahead of JPP in the 2010 draft.
           </p>
           <p>
            JPP plays on a defensive line with Justin Tuck and Osi Umenyiora (and dont forget Mathias Kiwanuka as a pass-rusher), and I think he will challenge the NFLs single-season sack record.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <blockquote class="twitter-tweet tw-align-center">
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>

             <a href="http://t.co/ODEpWIz5" title="http://www.nj.com/giants/index.ssf/2012/09/giants_jason_pierre-paul_think.html">
              nj.com/giants/index.s
             </a>
            </p>
            <p>
              Adam Schefter (@AdamSchefter)
             <a href="https://twitter.com/AdamSchefter/status/243280807488286720">
              September 5, 2012
             </a>
            </p>
           </blockquote>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Andy Reid Will Save His Job with a 12-4 Season
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Andy Reid Will Save His Job with a 12-4 Season" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/288/hi-res-151014458_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Zelevansky/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Philadelphia Eagles owner Jeffrey Lurie
            <a href="http://sports.yahoo.com/blogs/nfl-shutdown-corner/eagles-owner-vick-sets-tone-8-8-won-110901906--nfl.html">
             said the other day
            </a>
            that
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/andy-reid">
             Andy Reid
            </a>
            needs to go better than 8-8 to save his job.
           </p>
           <p>
            Realistically, thats not a ridiculous statement. If Reid cant win more than half his games
            <em>
             again
            </em>
            with this kind of talent, its time to move on. Sure, if Michael Vick goes down with an injury in Week 1, its a different storyand the fact that the offensive line is without All-Pro tackle Jason Peters hurts.
           </p>
           <p>
            However, LeSean McCoy, DeSean Jackson, Jeremy Maclin, Brent Celek and an unbelievable defensive line that could lead the NFL in sacks in 2012 should mean at least double-digit wins, even in a tough division and with the seventh-toughest schedule in the league. Ill say 12-4 and a deep playoff run.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-45 cf display-none " data-page="45">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Six Coaches Will Be Fired After the Season
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Six Coaches Will Be Fired After the Season" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/289/hi-res-150872171_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Zelevansky/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The National Football League sees a shocking turnover rate among its head coaches on an annual basis. Suffer through one losing season and you better improve quickly. Two in a row and youre definitely on the hot seat. Three means youre trying to get a coordinator job somewhere else.
           </p>
           <p>
            With that in mind, the following head coaches will be fired this season (with their teams predicted record in parentheses):
           </p>
           <p>
            Jason Garrett, Dallas Cowboys (8-8)
           </p>
           <p>
            Ken Whisenhunt, Arizona Cardinals (4-12)
           </p>
           <p>
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/rex-ryan">
             Rex Ryan
            </a>
            , New York Jets (5-11)
           </p>
           <p>
            Norv Turner, San Diego Chargers (8-8)
           </p>
           <p>
            Leslie Frazier, Minnesota Vikings (3-13)
           </p>
           <p>
            Pat Shurmur,
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1283529-cleveland-browns-roster-2012-latest-news-cuts-preseason-predictions">
             Cleveland Browns
            </a>
            (3-13)
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-46 cf display-none " data-page="46">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             NFC Playoff Teams
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="NFC Playoff Teams" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/290/hi-res-150454085_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jonathan Daniel/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <em>
             NFC East: New York Giants (12-4)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             NFC North: Green Bay Packers (13-3)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             NFC South: Atlanta Falcons (12-4)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             NFC West: Seattle Seahawks (9-7)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             <br/>
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Wild Card: Philadelphia Eagles (12-4)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Wild Card: Tampa Bay Buccaneers (10-6)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            I mentioned in an earlier slide that I think the Buccaneers will be a surprise success. I think the Chicago Bears will nearly make the playoffs (10-6), but I have them ultimately just missing out.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Dallas Cowboys and Detroit Lions will be average teams despite expectations that they will do well. I also have the San Francisco 49ers missing out, which will come as a surprise to many.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             AFC Playoff Teams
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="AFC Playoff Teams" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/291/hi-res-138677608_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Ezra Shaw/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <em>
             AFC East: New England Patriots (14-2)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             AFC North: Cincinnati Bengals (10-6)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             AFC South:
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1282868-houston-texans-roster-tracking">
              Houston Texans
             </a>
             (11-5)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             AFC West: Kansas City Chiefs (10-6)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Wild Card: Buffalo Bills (10-6)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Wild Card: Tennessee Titans (9-7)
            </em>
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            The big surprise here is the Pittsburgh Steelers and the Baltimore Ravens both missing the playoffs. As I wrote earlier, Im not a fan of either team heading into 2012.
           </p>
           <p>
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/ben-roethlisberger">
             Ben Roethlisberger
            </a>
            is a top-notch quarterback, but hes due to get hurt and miss substantial time behind that offensive line, and I dont think the Steelers can rely on
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/troy-polamalu">
             Troy Polamalu
            </a>
            to stay healthy or Mike Wallace to repeat his 2011 success after a lengthy holdout.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-48 cf display-none " data-page="48">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>

             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              48
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">

              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             NFC Championship Game
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="NFC Championship Game" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/292/hi-res-136322298_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Kevin C. Cox/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Everything in me wanted to pick the Green Bay Packers to make the conference championship game.
           </p>
           <p>
            From an NFL standpoint, I absolutely love the makeup of their teamAaron Rodgers is the best quarterback in the game, they have a pair of bookend tackles that should hold down the fort for the next decade and they have two tremendous receivers and an elite tight end in Greg Jennings, Jordy Nelson and Jermichael Finley respectively.
           </p>
           <p>
            However, they have too many problems on the defensive side of the ball. Dont forget this team gave up the most passing yards in NFL history in 2011, and they lost Nick Collins to retirement. Their running game is atrocious too.
           </p>
           <p>
            Instead, Im going with the Atlanta Falcons over the Packers in a surprise NFC Divisional Round upset, which puts the Falcons against the Philadelphia Eagles in a battle of the birds, with the winner going to the Super Bowl. This would be a rematch of the 2004 NFC championship Game, and it would put Michael Vick and Asante Samuel head-to-head against their old teams.
           </p>
           <p>
            I see Matt Ryan finally getting over the playoff hump that has plagued his career, and I see Andy Reid losing his fifth conference championship game.
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Final Score: Atlanta 24, Philadelphia 20
            </em>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             AFC Championship Game
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="AFC Championship Game" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/293/hi-res-137771087_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jim Rogash/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            I dont think the AFC is going to be very strong this season. I dont have perennial playoff contenders the Baltimore Ravens and Pittsburgh Steelers qualifying for January ball this year, and I really dont think theres anyone that can compete with the New England Patriots.
           </p>
           <p>
            In fact, I think the Patriots may finish with at least three more wins than any other AFC team. I have the Patriots squaring off against the Houston Texansa very solid football team with Matt Schaub healthy again, Andre Johnson healthy, Arian Foster, a terrific offensive line and a tremendous defense.
           </p>
           <p>
            However, Tom Brady and
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/bill-belichick">
             Bill Belichick
            </a>
            win this one easily, which puts them in their sixth Super Bowl in the past 12 years.
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Final Score: New England 38, Houston 20
            </em>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-50 cf display-none " data-page="50">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              50
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             The New England Patriots Will Win the Super Bowl
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="The New England Patriots Will Win the Super Bowl" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/294/hi-res-137565764_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Elsa/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            I think this will be a really good game. By this point in the season, I think Matt Ryan will have graduated from the kind-of-elite club with players like Tony Romo, Philip Rivers and Jay Cutler to the definitely elite club.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Atlanta Falcons will give the New England Patriots lots of trouble with Roddy White, Julio Jones and Tony Gonzalez, but then again, the Patriots can counter with Wes Welker, Brandon Lloyd, Rob Gronkowski and Aaron Hernandez.
           </p>
           <p>
            Im sure Asante Samuel will record a pick against his old team (by the way, would he be the first Pro Bowl player ever to play his former teams in the conference championship game and the Super Bowl in the same season?), but the Patriots offense will just be too much.
           </p>
           <p>
            <em>
             Final Score: New England 34, Atlanta 24
            </em>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-51 cf display-none " data-page="51">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              51
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">
               52
              </span>
             </div>
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Next Page">
              Next
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
             </a>
            </div>
            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             And Who Else but Tom Brady Will Win the Games MVP?
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="And Who Else but Tom Brady Will Win the Games MVP?" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/563/295/hi-res-137771198_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jim Rogash/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            If you found out the New England Patriots were going to win the Super Bowl, the odds of Tom Brady winning the games MVP award would probably be at least 75 percent.
           </p>
           <p>
            Sure, it could be Rob Gronkowski, Aaron Hernandez, Wes Welker or even a defensive player, but the Patriots are a passing team that will put up a ton of points, and this game could cement Bradys reputation as the greatest quarterback who ever lived.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
        </div>
